< Review>
I wanted to buy a deluxe edition of a game that wasn't being sold anywhere but at this specific Gamestop, so I called ahead to reserve and they said they'll hold it for a day. I visit around the afternoon with a friend to pick up the game, only to be told that it was out of stock. I literally wasted 50 minutes of my life driving to this place from the desert, only to find that the game I reserved had been given to someone else.

So despite my disappointment I decided to just get the regular edition....I mean, Im not the type to stay angry about things, plus I know that computers don't reflect something is in stock or not on time, (except wait, I forgot, I CALLED the place and they said they would have it for me,
and they didn't!!!)....... all the while, the employee that was helping me that day somehow had the audacity to tell me in a sarcastic manner that it was MY fault for not pre-ordering, or that I should ALWAYS pre-order games (tip: if you preorder games, there's a high chance the price will be lowered some time later for a sale, or they'll have an extra edition in the future, with all its dlcs and extras at half the cost. I don't recommend preordering, I already learned my lesson the first time. You all decide what you want to do with your life.)Then, after we made the transaction, he starts reading off a list of games that I could pre-order in a super-demanding attitude, like "you better pre-order now or else," and it honestly took me aback. Did someone not make your coffee right today, or are you just a natural asshat? Also, are we forgetting the fact that YOU were the one who told me via phone that my copy was reserved, only to give it away? I should NOT be blamed for your mistake & SURELY not in such a rude manner. You could have just told me politely that I could try pre-ordering, but no, you insulted me and made me feel like an idiot, when you were the one with the problem!

This is my first and last time visiting this Gamestop. There are better gamestops out there who treat their customers better, unlike this one.<//Review>

< Review>
A friend of mine referred me to United Fitness, so I thought I'd give it a try.  I have been unmotivated because of long work hours and little time and as a result, I have a lot more fat on my body than normal.  The thought of being able to lose at least 4% body fat in just 6 weeks and the fact that I only need to work out about 35 minutes a day excited me. The first moment I stepped inside, my mouth dropped.  The paint job on the walls are amazing and the music makes me want to dance nonstop.  This is definitely way better than any other gym or fitness club I've been to.  It's much more fun, but they're serious about getting you the results you're looking for. While scrolling though facebook one day I came across a post which stated I could lose 20 pounds for free. Usually one would assume when seeing this that this is some kind of scam or there has to be a catch. Since the gym was right down the street from me I thought why not just send an email and see what happens. I was contacted pretty shortly after and asked if I could come in for a consultation.

Upon arriving to the gym I was greeted and the first thing I noticed how spacious and new everything was. The gym also had some of my favorite work out items such as sleds, kettle bells and free weights. I was informed a deposit was required to motivate people. It made sense to me. I could see people giving up after a week but if you had money on the line people would be inclined to really give it their all.

At first I though the deposit was a bit steep and I compared it to my big box gym where I paid 30 a month. I decided nothing ventured nothing gained so I signed up.

The one good thing I can say about "upgrades" to downtown Morgan Hill is that we have been blessed by an improved selection dinning choices and Opa is one that heads the list.
- We've always had a great meal here. We tend to make it to Opa's for an early dinner so we slot-in easily between the official Lunch/Dinner crowds giving us  our choice of table (hence I can't say from experience how peak hour dinning there is but I'd think it is packed so I expect reservations would be wise). <rating>3</rating>< text>
I've been coming to NoCal a lot this year as I'm really relating back to my San Francisco hometown roots.

After my cousin picked me up at San Jose Airport we're both hungry and settled on Morgan Hill for lunch. Wanting to go to Willard Hicks we settled on Opa as WH was closed.

Opa is an attractive restaurant. The outdoor seating area is lovely, the indoor bar is complete and the staff is incredibly nice. The Greek menu has all of the regulars along with their own take on certain dishes. I loved their Greek themed Beet Salad. It had all of the components of true Greek flavors. As it was, good is good. And in the Yelp World, good = 3 Stars.</text>

Awesome place to do amateur astronomy late at night.   Gate in closes at 8pm, but you can leave whenever. If you are night hikers or whatever, and you see us there in the West contact station parking lot, please dim or turn off your lights, you're welcome to visit us in the dark but with your lights on you can't see through our telescopes.  National park fees or passes required.</text>

<Name>Clinton Lee< /Name><Time>1539299937718< /Time>< Rate>

<Text>We were heading North on 101 and had a few hours to spare, so we made an unplanned stop here.  First off, the cave and the views were beautiful and we were really happy we stopped.  Reminded me of the Black Hills of South Dakota.  Except with Condors.
However, on October 11, the visitor center was closed and the park was not staffed, although the roads, trails, and bathrooms were open. Also, there is no mobile phone service there. So if you were (like me) too dumb to download the park map ahead of time, you are on you own.  I took a picture of the map posted at the West trail head, and we were then able to find our way into and out of the Balconies cave and cliff trails.
My advice is fire up your phone before you leave Soledad, and download the park map and maybe a Google map of the area too.< /Text><pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOBlAU8LVszDzya3RttcmymjaZFyRu6UlDlNoXr=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures><resp>None</resp><gmap_id>0x809243b644eda78f:0x3c7ce0591d514f6e< /gmap_id></record>

< Review>
The Bar: Located in Orange, on Chapman Avenue across from the local high school. In a strip mall, with a Del Taco within walking distance which is especially nice when wasted. Approaching the bar, there is a single door into a dark room. The bar itself is oddly shaped, sorta like a boomerang. First thing ya notice walking in, is the liquor, conveniently placed near the door to attract the consumer.
The Crowd: Well, this night, it was pretty dead inside. We ran into another bartender from Marty's Cocktails out partying with her friends, so we decided to kick it at that end of the bar. As for the rest of the crowd... there were a couple of old dudes at the bar, and a couple on the pool tables.. that was about it.
Service: Prompt, but the bar was empty.
Prices: From what I can remember, I believe it was $2.75 a bottle for domestic, and $5.50 a shot for Jameson, yet no PBR.
Entertainment: 2 pool tables, bar top video game, dart board, a few TV's.
Restroom: I almost don't need to write about this disgusting area. Look at the picture below. It smelled worse that in looks, if that's even possible.
Bartender: Poison pusher for the night was Teri. From what we've heard, she is legen....wait for it....dary. Would not disagree with that statement. Made for a great time.
Closing statement: Besides being on a major street with lots of Cops, not too bad. Had a great time, with great people and certainly plan on making a return trip in the near future.</Review>

Walter Macalma</Name>
< Date>
1402702950304</Date>
<rating>2< /rating>< Text>
This is highly unlike me to visit once and review, but as a warning I will not be returning. I only went here because I couldn't find Blondies trying to grab a drink before an event in the area.

Cash only, ATM inside. Dingy sticky gummy carpet, dark from not having any windows. Poor lighting is probably a good thing so you don't see things you don't want to. 2 Beers on tap and a dozen in bottles. Strong makers and coke. Cheap bottle of Newcastle. The coke was poured from a bottle and not from a speed tap, that's pretty hood and the beers are the real value. The smell reminded me of those old dessert dive bar in Nevada way way way of the strip, a mixture of sweat and cleaner. The bar itself is shapped interesting.

A dozen stools around the bar and pool tables in the back. I didn't use the restroom because I had 2 drinks and bounced. They were folding bar towels as I came in. I was digging the internal stained glass hidden window thingy and the old school cash register. Service was a little slow, but nothing bad, just 1 bartender for a HH swing in a pretty empty bar. I was totally used to the Cumbia music blaring as well as the cheesy fluorescent writing on the black board. T-Mobile 4g service was good inside. Parking is limited up front and even more so on the sides and back.

Dive and nothing more. I prefer a dive with more variety to stand, sit, maybe a patio, some windows, better tv's, better music, but most importantly beer on tap. I'm not a bottle drinking and that coke from a 2 liter bottle was the straw for me.</Text>

<review>This awesome little eatery tucked away into the corner could be easily missed while driving on La Cienega. By the first look of it, I did not notice much people eating at the restaurant but once we ordered the food and as it arrives after a little wait, it was all worth it.

<name>Karen Kurokawa<//name><Time>1557552825866</Time><rate>5</rate><Review>This wonderful family-owned restaurant serves familiar Middle Eastern dishes but with a Jordanian touch that elevates them above their competitors.  They also have a few Jordanian specialty entrees every night from among those listed on the Twagen section of the menu.  Tonight's Bamiya (lamb shank with okra in a light tomato sauce was excellent.  Their slow baked, sophisticatedly seasoned chicken Musakhan is also worth seeking out. I order it with rice instead of pita because I have celiac disease.  Their tender, cardomom-scented rice definitely not a second-best! By the way, I am a ful mudammas fan, and there is no doubt that the ful at Oasis is the best I've eaten in Los Angeles.  It is served warm and mashed, topped with tahini sauce, good olive oil, chopped tomatoes, and a few spots of excellent house-made green hot sauce.  If you enjoy spicing up your food, you can ask for some extra hot sauce to go with it, though I think it is perfection just the way it arrives.  The service is warm and friendly, and if you have celiac disease and/or food intolerances, they will help to to eat safely and feel welcome.< /Review>< Pics>

<review>When I come to Bishop and crave a good Mexican dinner, it's always La Casita! The chips and salsa are great basic starters. The restaurant makes their own salsa and offers two types: mild (for wimps) and hot. Tell 'em to bring the hot... and don't worry, they'll bring plenty more if needed. Their salsa is a sort of chunky style with diced tomatoes, onions, cilantro etc. Yum! Oh, and make sure to order a Modelo Especial (Cerveza) or two to enjoy with your appetizer and main course. The cheese and beef enchiladas are delicious, as are their many other menu options. Everything is fresh and tasty, you'll never leave hungry!

Despite reading some other reviews, I've always received top-notch service here, never had any problems. Their servers are always prompt and courteous! There's an adjacent bar next to the restaurant. If you're only looking for drinks and relaxation, maybe watch some sports games, you have that available here too.

When you're in Bishop, make plans to stop by La Casita for a delicious Mexican meal!</review><Pics>None</Pics><Response>None< /Response><Gmap_id>0x80be3dfe6539e537:0xc72a8fc4223868c2< /Gmap_id></record>

Our bill came to almost $700. and we were all very disappointed in the steaks.  We all ordered the New York Steaks and all at the table complained as the steaks were laced with the silver skin through the meat which is simply unchewable and wrecks an otherwise good meal.  I purchase prime steaks from all over the country and consider Kansas City New York steaks at the very entry level bottom of the prime food chain, in fact I refuse to ever order them again.
I can‚Äôt understand why the Dutch Ftontier is not ordering and serving the best, especially considering what they charge for their dinners.  Allen Brothers, Stockyards, and Pat LaFreida to name a few supply restaurant quality prime steaks to restaurants and they are all so much better than Kansas City Steaks.    I‚Äôd much rather pay more and get more!
The evening was nice, service was good, corkage fee rather pricey, and entree a big disappointment!
I won‚Äôt be back unless they change meat suppliers!<//text>

<rate>5</rate></record></dataset><record>
<rate>1</rate>< text>
I needed service for my Goodman furnace over a weekend and this company was able to come on Sunday for a service call fee of just $69.99 (applicable to any repair charges).  The technician arrived timely and was both personable and efficient.  After a 10-15 minute check of my system, he diagnosed the problem as a "defective high limit thermostat," the repair of which required ordering a "high limit thermostat kit" from Goodman at a total cost of $400 (including the $70 service fee already paid).  I thought this was high, told the tech I'd wanted to get other estimates and that I would contact the office if I wanted to go forward.  I then spent some time on YouTube and learned: (1) That the small part in question is a specialized switch (not a "kit") which installs with one screw and can be ordered online from multiple vendors for ~$6 + shipping;  (2) How to easily test whether my part was defective using an ohm meter (I did that and determined that the part was not defective); and (3) That the commonest cause my specific problem was a clogged air filter.  So, I reinserted the same switch, reconnected it to its 2 wires, replaced the air filter (even though it appeared to be ok), turned the furnace on and discovered that --- it now works just fine.  Anyone reading this review should  consider whether this is an appliance repair company they wish to engage.</text>

< Text>
Had a service technician over on 11/20/15 to diagnose problems with my professional range. He seemed very professional and diagnosed the problems swiftly. However, I was a bit stunned when told the repairs would be $1750. As I glanced over the Invoice, I realized the numbers did not add up. I took out my calculator and found a discrepancy of over $300 in his addition. He quickly wrote up a new quote for $1418 and stated he would have the parts in plenty of time for Thanksgiving.

Realizing the urgency to get my range repaired before the holiday, I happily wrote a check for $425 to cover the required deposit. The technician stated the parts would arrive in 1-2 business days and that he would return Monday or Tuesday. I was delighted! (Note: I live in a gated community so I was able to get the technicians cell phone number to buzz him in the gate)

After waiting around all day Monday for a call to schedule the repair, I called the office. They stated that all the parts were in and that the technician would be out between 2-5pm Tuesday. Needing the repairs done before my 15 guests arrived Wednesday to celebrate the holiday, I took the day off work and waited....and waited....and waited! I finally called the technician at 6pm to find out why he had not shown up. He stated he was stuck in traffic and his GPS was indicating 2.5 hours to my home but that he would try to make it out.

Needless to say, he never made it or called me back. I promptly called the company early Wednesday morning to reschedule. They stated the technician would arrive no later than 11am. So again, I took the day off work and waited. At 1pm I became concerned when I again heard nothing from the technician so I placed several calls to his cell and the company. Finally, at about 5pm, the technician called back and stated that he had locked his keys in the car and is unable to keep the appointment. I then placed a call back to the company and was told someone would call me back when they got it figured out. About 1.5 hours later, the company called to inform me that they would have the technician out to my home the next day, THANKSGIVING, and guaranteed to get the range fixed. I was told I would be the first service call and that the technician would arrive between 8-10am.

With 15 guests at my home and no working range, I took them out to dinner and just prayed that I could catch up on Thanksgiving dinner once the repairs were done.

Thanksgiving day arrives but not the technician! After several calls, I finally reached the technician. He stated he was on his way & would arrive in 25 minutes. After waiting almost 2 hours, I again started calling when the technician was a no show. About a hour later, a supervisor called and I was told that the main part needed to repair my range, the thermostat, arrived but that the wrong part was in the box so the part would have to be reordered and the appointment would have to be rescheduled in 1-2 business days. This seemed odd because the technician was clearly driving when I spoke to him on his cell. Did he pull over to check the parts on his way?

I was left with no choice but to use the broken range to prepare my Thanksgiving dinner for 15 guests. It wasn't easy rotating everything between the one small oven that worked and the BBQ but with some stress and prayers we were able to finally enjoy our Thanksgiving dinner....at 8pm!

Its now Wednesday, December 2, and I still have not heard back from the company. I called today and demanded to speak to a supervisor. I wasn't surprised when told the supervisors aren't in, they come and go daily, but that someone would call me back within 24 hours.

I give up! Thanks Reliable Appliance Service, Inc for your completely unreliable service & dishonesty!

Next step....stop payment on my $425 deposit and call Pacific Sales!<//Text>
